![Schünemann Storms to Victory in Ghent!](https://media.magic.wizards.com/images/banner/large_1_4.jpg)





Grand Prix Ghent 2012
---------------------


Schünemann Storms to Victory in Ghent!
======================================




July 21-22, 2012












Grand Prix Ghent 2012
---------------------


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/Timo%20Schunemann%20Grand%20Prix%20Ghent%20Champion.jpg)


Congratulations to Timo Schünemann the Grand Prix Ghent 2012 Champion!


Looking at the top eight of this Legacy Grand Prix here in Belgium, there was always the potential of a lightning fast final, with a number of combo decks still in the running. The crowd were not disappointed, with an all-German final of Elves vs Storm inevitably leading to some quick games.


When the dust settled it was Schünemann holding the trophy, winning the match in a flurry of ritual effects, culminating in a sizeable [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony). All weekend we've seen Legacy to be a diverse and high powered format. Whether casting [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) to sneak some of the most formidable permanents in the game into play, or resolving double digits of spells in a single turn with any manner of combo decks, Legacy shows off the best of the history of **Magic**. Our top eight included seven distinct archetypes and, in a distinct departure from many recent results, not a single copy of [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets). In spite of RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) being the most played deck in the room, it seemed that other options were able to take down the deck that won in Atlanta, with a variety of other options including Maverick, various [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) decks and even Lands finishing high up in the standings.


*M13* has made its presence known, with Merfolk and Goblins each getting a shot in the arm with a new powerful creature, and in addition to this [Omniscience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Omniscience) saw its first significant tournament play as a new piece in the [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) puzzle.


As the sun sets on the Grand Prix here in Ghent, and attentions almost certainly turn to the two Grand Prix happening on the other side of the Atlantic, there will be one man content to rest on his laurels, and be the first of three this weekend travelling home with a trophy. That man is Timo Schünemann, our Grand Prix champion!


Top 8 bracket
-------------






### Quaterfinals





(1) Schünemann, Timo




(8) Tristan, Polzl






(4) Klocker, Elias




(5) Watsfeldt, Elias






(2) Sjoblom, Max




(7) Maurer, Lukas






(3) Marcotti, Emanuele




(6) Milillo, Andrea







### Semi-finals





**Schünemann, Timo 2-0**




Watsfeldt, Elias 2-1






**Maurer, Lukas 2-0**




Marcotti, Emanuele 2-0







### Finals





**Schünemann, Timo 2-1**




Maurer, Lukas 2-1







### Champion





**Schünemann, Timo 2-1**

Top 8 Profiles
--------------


*by Event Coverage Staff* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_sj%C3%B6blom.jpg)

### Max Sjöblom


**Age:** 24  


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_maurer.jpg)

### Lukas Maurer


**Age:** 27  
**Hometown:** Munich, Germany  
**Occupation:** Student

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

Getting labeled as "Manface" by the Grand Prix Amsterdam coverage staff.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  

Combo Elves. Experience with the deck, plus I think it's amongst the best decks.


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  
[Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Linvala%2C+Keeper+of+Silence) gives the deck a hard time, so maybe [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) in the sideboard.


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**  
[Badlands](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Badlands).





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_p%C3%B6lzl.jpg)

### Tristan Pölzl


**Age:** 24  
**Hometown:** Montreuil, France  
**Occupation:** None

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

Top 8 at Bazaar of Moxen 6.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  

Junk Souls, because it has [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary)!


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  

No changes. Already the best list!


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**  
[Omniscience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Omniscience).





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_sch%C3%BCnemann.jpg)

### Timo Schünemann


**Age:** 25  
**Hometown:** Solingen, Germany  
**Occupation:** Student

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

Winning a piece of the Power Nine.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  

UBr [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) because Dredge betrayed me.


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  

I wouldn't change a thing.


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**  
[Smokestack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smokestack).





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_watsfeldt.jpg)

### Elias Watsfeldt


**Age:** 19  
**Hometown:** Gothenburg, Sweden  
**Occupation:** Student

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

Gold level! Reigning Swedish Legacy champion.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  
[Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell). Because it allows you to consistently get [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn)/[Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) on turn three.


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  

Plus two [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) in the sideboard against Maverick and Reanimator. Otherwise I'm ambivalent about the sideboard because I did not draw Jace and [Bitterblossom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bitterblossom) very often.


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**  
[Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Linvala%2C+Keeper+of+Silence) against my [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand), [Surgical Extraction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surgical+Extraction) against my reanimation spells.





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_klocker.jpg)

### Elias Klocker


**Age:** 18  
**Hometown:** [Austria]  
**Occupation:** Student

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

Top 32 at Grand Prix Turin.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  

GW Maverick


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  

Probably cut the [Sword of Light and Shadow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Light+and+Shadow).


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**  
[Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) because Scavenging Ooze beat it every time.





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_marcotti.jpg)

### Emanuele Marcotti


**Age:** 23  
**Hometown:** Castelvetro Piacentino, Italy  
**Occupation:** Student

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

It's my first Grand Prix. I only play local Eternal events.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  

Stoneblade with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) because my brother has had good results with it recently.


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  

None.


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**  
[Withered Wretch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Withered+Wretch).





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_t8_milillo.jpg)

### Andrea Milillo


**Age:** 24  
**Hometown:** Mozzate, Italy  
**Occupation:** Student

**Previous **Magic** accomplishments:**   

It's my first Grand Prix, and I only played in one PTQ.


**What deck did you play and why did you choose it?**  

Landstill, because no one wants to trade for my three [Standstill](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Standstill)s.


**What changes would you make to your deck and why would you make them?**  

None. I would switch decks.


**What was the most unusual card that was played against you this weekend?**

[Horizon Canopy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+[Horizon]+[Canopy])

76 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Cavern+of+Souls)



















Quarterfinal - Elias Klocker vs. Elias Watsfeldt
------------------------------------------------


*by Rich Hagon* 
My desire to caption this one as 'The Elias Sports Bureau Presents' is enormous, but since only three of you reading this will understand the reference, I've decided against it. Instead, let's get to the action, with the two Eliaseseses facing each other with a place at the Pro Tour at stake for one of them, Mr. Klocker. Yesterday, Watsfeldt was on the verge of missing out on day two.


"My friend told me that if I didn't make day two, we could go to Paris today to see the last stage of the Tour de France. I don't think I like cycling. I decided that I had better start winning."


Now Watsfeldt finds himself in his second GP top 8, following a quarter final appearance at GP San Diego late last year. Klocker, meanwhile, is in his first elimination match in front of such a big crowd, and a win here would get him the coveted invite to Pro Tour Return to Ravnica in Seattle later this year.


### Game 1


After a mulligan to 6, Klocker opened on [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch). Watsfeldt converted [Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats) into a straightforward [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp), and used [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) to reveal a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), [Savannah](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Savannah), [Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant), and [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch). The Hierarch hit the graveyard. [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) was next from Watsfeldt, who took Elspeth, seeing a freshly-drawn [Scryb Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scryb+Ranger) for Klocker. [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) was imprinted with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), with [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) ending the turn, leaving Klocker to flash in [Scryb Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scryb+Ranger).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/Ghent_quarter_watsfeldt.jpg)

*Elias Watsfeldt* 
He added a second [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch), then watched Watsfeldt cast [Lim-Dûl's Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lim-D%C3%BBl%27s+Vault) at end of turn. He plowed his way down to 6 life before he was satisfied with the set of 5 cards from the Vault. That set the stage for an [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn) turn, presumably...


Yep. [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell). [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn). Good game.


Klocker 0 - 1 Watsfeldt


### Game 2


Both players kept their opening 7 for game 2, with [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) from Watsfeldt the first action. Turn two saw [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) from Klocker. Watsfeldt wasted no time fetching [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) from [Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats). He laid [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox), imprinting [Personal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Personal+Tutor), and cast [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), revealing [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn)...


[Submerge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Submerge) cleared the way, but Klocker wasn't done, using [Crop Rotation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crop+Rotation) to find [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas). That's quite good against [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn), apparently. With Emrakil now back in hand, Watsfeldt had to regroup. Klocker flashed out [Scryb Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scryb+Ranger), then started his turn with [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) for [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea). Watsfeldt fell to a still-manageable 15 with the attack. [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) for his [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) stunted his mana further. He cast [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) to take away [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), while Klocker took his chance to get [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) onto the board.


[Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben) was next, as the Klocker attacks gathered momentum, thanks to the Jitte. Despite a turn two [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn), that [Crop Rotation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crop+Rotation) for [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) had saved the day for Klocker, and forced a deciding game 3.


Klocker 1 - 1 Watsfeldt.


### Game 3


Both players thought hard about their 7s before keeping. Watsfeldt used [Personal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Personal+Tutor) for [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) on turn one, Klocker replying with [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch). After drawing the [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), Watsfeldt laid a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp), and passed. Watsfeldt looked surprised when Klocker passed without a turn two play. Watsfeldt aimed for [Lim-Dûl's Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lim-D%C3%BBl%27s+Vault) at end of turn, which Klocker nodded through. How good a hand could Watsfeldt construct from his 'favorite five'?



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_quarter_klocker.jpg)

*Elias Klocker* 
It didn't take him long. [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) imprinted [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) landed [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) for Klocker, and [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) for Watsfeldt. Klocker went for [Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor), and saw [Submerge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Submerge) return his [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). He replayed it, and attacked Watsfeldt to 17. Another [Submerge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Submerge) sent the Knight packing, and it was all over.


Elias Klocker 1 - 2 Elias Watsfeldt



Semifinal - Timo Schünemann vs. Elias Watsfeldt
-----------------------------------------------


*by Rich Hagon* 
Legacy, you may have heard, is quite a powerful format, where some seriously nutty things go on. If you have heard this, you are not wrong, and if you haven't, you're about to find out how true that is, as both Schünemann and Watsfeldt have some pretty saucy things on the docket.


### Game 1


Schünemann opened the semi final with [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe), finding two [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress), [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), [Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats), [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn), [Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Catacombs), and [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta). Schünemann turned his own [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) into [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea). [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) took [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), leaving the two [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) to Watsfeldt. [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) number one revealed [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony), [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy), [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish), and two land. Unsurprisingly, it was the [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish) that hit the graveyard. Back came [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) from Schünemann, taking away the second [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress). [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) saw Watsfeldt leave the cards on top, before [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) reset the top of the deck. [Personal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Personal+Tutor) for [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) completed a solid turn.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/Ghent_semi_watsfeldt.jpg)

*Elias Watsfeldt* 
[Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats) became a third [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea) for Watsfeldt, who cast [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), revealing [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) opposite nothing but land for Schünemann. Three sacs later, he had a very different lineup of lands, but they were still, you know, lands. [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony) was hardcast, taking Schünemann a miniscule amount of life further from death. After [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) smashed him extremely hard in the face, he cast [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). Then [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal). Then [Dark Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Ritual). Then [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor). He found [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames), but Watsfeldt showed [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) at the ready.


Schünemann 0 - 1 Watsfeldt


### Game 2


[Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) let Schünemann see two [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn), [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox), and an [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea). Away went [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), leaving Watsfeldt to start the game with [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) imprinting [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), plus the [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea). Schünemann didn't get to [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) either, Watsfeldt opting to cast [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), pitching the second [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). Why quickly became clear, as he cast [Lim-Dûl's Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lim-D%C3%BBl%27s+Vault) at end of turn. With two [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) gone, could he get past the Schünemann defence? [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) from Schünemann saw land and [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn) in hand - the [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) was up second from the Vault.


Schünemann now had to go for it. He cast two [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond), then [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam). 19, 17, 13 off [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames), 11 [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish), 10 [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), 8 [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish), 7 [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe), 5 [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor), 4 [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) - 'nom nom nom nom nom'. That wasn't Watsfeldt saying that...


Schünemann completed the proscribed endgame, and we were tied at one.


Schünemann 1 - 1 Watsfeldt


### Game 3


Watsfeldt kept 7, while Schünemann quickly sent his back. He kept 6.


[Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) imprinting [Personal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Personal+Tutor) was Watsfeldt's opening, with [Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Catacombs). [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) was met with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) in response, allowing Watsfeldt to hide [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) and [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) on top of his library before the [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) could resolve. When it did, Schünemann found [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress), and a [Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats) in hand, with the [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) getting taken. Watsfeldt went straight into [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), of course, revealing [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus). Schünemann chose not to reveal, and the play passed to the German.



![](http://media.wizards.com/legacy/migration/GHENT_final_schunemann.jpg)

*Timo Schünemann* 
He cast [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), with a lot of options in hand. Next was [Dark Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Ritual), with Schünemann confident of victory - 'I'm trying to decide how to kill you...'. [Cabal Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Ritual) followed, then [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond), [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor) for another [Cabal Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Ritual) (now with threshold), then flashback [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames)...


You know the rest. Storm...spell..storm...more storm... spell...[Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress)...storm... mana... Christmas...storm...Tuesday...


[Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony).


Kill you.


Told you Legacy was a powerful format.


Timo Schünemann 2 - 1 Elias Watsfeldt

Semifinal - Emanule Marcotti vs. Lukas Maurer
---------------------------------------------


*by Tim Willoughby* 
Any time there is an Italian in the top 8 of a Grand Prix there is quite a crowd, and with Emanuele Marcotti here now, it was no different. His Esper Stoneblade deck was up against the elves deck of Lukas Maurer of Germany, and if he won, he would be facing Timo Schünemann, also of Germany, but playing a different combo deck in Storm.


### Game 1


A turn one [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) saw [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest), [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers), three copies of [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger), [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote) and [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary). The Symbiote hit the bin, and Marcotti passed, challenging Maurer to do his worst. A [Fyndhorn Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fyndhorn+Elves) came off the top and straight into play as the most straightforward form of acceleration the German could go for.


A turn two [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) from Marcotti fetched... well, nothing.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_semi_maurer.jpg)

*Lukas Maurer* 
"A little bit unlucky" remarked Marcotti, who already had both [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) and [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) in hand.


Maurer was quick to take any shot he could, and used [Fyndhorn Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fyndhorn+Elves), [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger) and [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers) to get mana to cast [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) – a quickly deployed squad ready to do something special.



![Ezuri, Renegade Leader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Ezuri%2C+Renegade+Leader)

Marcotti cast [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), seeing Thoughtsezie [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). He thought for a little (appropriate considering he was casting [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)) and stacked things such that [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) was on top, to remain safe against anything too explosive from his opponent.


A [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for one resolved, fetching [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote). The Symbiote would let Maurer bounce and recast his [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary), but Marcotti was not about to let the German get too crazy. When Visionary came back, it was hit by [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) from Marcotti left Maurer with just a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest).


While Marcotti's [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) had yet to deploy any equipment, the threat of it doing so was enough to keep Maurer honest about entering the red zone. Maurer cast another [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith), this time finding [Ezuri, Renegade Leader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ezuri%2C+Renegade+Leader). Now he would have an attacking force to be reckoned with.


Marcotti got his [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) on, but was looking in ropey shape to team Elf. [Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid) would be an efficient source of mana, but Maurer felt no need to rush things.


As [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) entered the battlefield for Marcotti, and got equipped to the [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) Germ, it looked that Marcotti was pulling ahead. In reality he wasn't getting far at all though, as [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote) could bounce Maurer's blocker, meaning that neither lifelink, nor Jitte's triggers would happen.


Marcotti looked to the sky. "[Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares)! I need it!"


It was Maurer who had the better draws though, with [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) which would be a veritable card drawing machine, especially once he found a second [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote). The game wasn't over, but it clearly wasn't far off. "I give up" declared Marcotti, scooping up his cards.


"I'll take it" muttered Maurer. He went 1-0 up.


Lukas Maurer 1 – 0 Emanuele Marcotti


### Game 2


The Italian's luck with his second opener was not great, but at least neither was Maurer's. Both players took a mulligan. While Marcotti's six card hand was keepable, the same could not be said of his opponent, who went to five.


That five soon became four, as Thoughseize saw [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor), [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature), [Viridian Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viridian+Shaman), [Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid) and [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote). The Glimpse went away, leaving an unexplosive hand for Maurer to work with. His turn one [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor) was unable to even tap for mana as it came in, and Marcotti was decisive in declaring "Jitte" as soon as he cast [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). Time to take control of things.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_semi_marcotti.jpg)

*Emanuele Marcotti* 
[Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote) came from Maurer, who took an attack before losing the insect to [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger) was the next play from Maurer, which was the perfect answer to Marcotti's [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) in the short term. The Ranger would let Maurer block and bounce with [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor) to keep Jitte from gaining counters, at the expense of missing land drops.


This plan would be fine for a while, but sooner or later Maurer would have to do something else, as his board would not be developing. Marcotti forced the issue with [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) on [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger).


Soon later Maurer was left in the awkward position of wanting to scoop up his cards, but being unable to due to not having any permanents, as [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) killed off his lone land.


Lukas Maurer 1 – 1 Emanuele Marcotti


### Game 3


The largely Italian crowd was at this point doing Mexican waves while celebrating the win, eager to see their countryman lock up a finals slot. For the rubber game, both players kept, and Maurer started with [Pendelhaven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pendelhaven) and [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel).


[Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) saw [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger), [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers), [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel), Scavenging Ooze and [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor). [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger) went away, but Maurer was still going to have quite a spicy turn, attacking in with his first [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel), before using it and [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers) to cast his second one.



![Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Nettle+Sentinel)

Marcotti cast [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), seeing an unexciting [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) and [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). He shuffled them away, instead getting a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). Maurer cast an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) using his [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel)s, before attacking with his team. A [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) got rid of one [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel), but even so, Marcotti was at 10 life from straightforward beatdowns.


Marcotti did not have a play for the turn, and looked on as [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle) further enabled Maurer to explode out of the gates. Attacks from Maurer were met with [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), allowing a flashback on [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), to remove [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary). The Mage did not block, and after combat Maurer had a [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle) naming [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte).


[Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) from Marcotti found [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), and Marcotti passed, on just 8 life, but with the potential to gain some back with his equipment given appropriate time. A [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) from Maurer resolved. From here came [Fyndhorn Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fyndhorn+Elves), Scavenging Ooze, [Llanowar Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Llanowar+Elves), [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary), [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote), [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) (again thanks to the Symbiote), a second [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature), [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary)...


At this point Marcotti had seen enough. He stood up and extended his hand, and with a round of applause Lukas Maurer advanced to the finals.


Lukas Maurer wins 2-1, advancing to what will be an all combo finals!



Final - Timo Schünemann vs. Lukas Maurer
----------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke* 
In this all-German final, Timo Schünemann, playing in his first Top 8, and his [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) storm combo deck were up against Elf player Lukas Maurer, likewise in his first Top 8.


### Game 1


Schünemann had earned the right to go first by virtue of his Swiss finish and did so, keeping his opening seven. Maurer did not, but was fine with six. However, it might not actually be six, as Schünemann started with [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) naming [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature). The Therapy missed but showed a hand of [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest), [Priest of Titania](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Priest+of+Titania), [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers), two copies of [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary), and [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith). The latter was then used by Maurer to go get [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor).


Schünemann, happy in the knowledge that it would be at least some time before Maurer's Elves could pose a serious threat, cast [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), which revealed that Maurer had found a lucky [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle) on top of his library. Maurer lost his [Priest of Titania](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Priest+of+Titania), but ripped [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) from the top of his deck and cast it. Down came [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers), followed by [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle) tapping for two (thanks to [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor) and the Rangers) to cast [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary), followed by [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger) untapping [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers), followed by [Fyndhorn Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fyndhorn+Elves).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpgnt12/GHENT_final_maurer.jpg)

*Lukas Maurer* 
[Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) and [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) gave Schünemann the cards he needed, both in hand as well as a seventh in his graveyard. "Finally," he commented. [Dark Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Ritual) was chained into [Cabal Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Ritual), followed by two [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal)s and an [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor) hellbent on destruction. Schünemann got [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames), with enough mana floating in his pool to cast it. After that it was all but over. Schünemann flashed back a couple of cards to generate even more mana, re-used [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor) to find [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony), and pointed the card (and all eleven of its storm copies) at Maurer's head.


Timo Schünemann 1 – 0 Lukas Maurer


### Game 2


Maurer had [Pendelhaven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pendelhaven) and [Fyndhorn Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fyndhorn+Elves) on turn one. His opponent's [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) revealed a hand of two more lands, [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature), [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel), and [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary). Schünemann followed it up with [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) getting rid of [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature). Maurer summoned [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) plus [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel) and passed the turn.


Schünemann, on his second turn, cast [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) and was ready to combo. He cast [Dark Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Ritual) off [Badlands](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Badlands) to pay for [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor), revealing one [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond) from his hand. The Tutor turned that into two Diamonds, which he played along with one [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal). The Petal allowed him to cast a second [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor) to which he responded by sacrificing both Diamonds. Now hellbent, the Tutor searched up [Ill-Gotten Gains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ill-Gotten+Gains).



![Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek)![Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Infernal+Tutor)

In response to [Ill-Gotten Gains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ill-Gotten+Gains), however, Maurer used [Faerie Macabre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faerie+Macabre) to remove the two [Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor)s from Schünemann's graveyard. "I really didn't expect that," Schünemann admitted. His options what to get back from his graveyard were reduced to [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal), one [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond), and [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder). [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) missed and Schünemann was forced to pass the turn to Maurer who now had his [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) back in hand thanks to [Ill-Gotten Gains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ill-Gotten+Gains).


Glimpse and lots of creatures followed, among them multiples of [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel), [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote), and [Quirion Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Quirion+Ranger), the latter two instrumental in allowing Maurer to keep going. Unfortunately, he couldn't find a single [Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid) or [Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers) and had to pass back to Schünemann. However, after this thwarted combo attempt, the storm player was down to a single card in hand and was simply overrun by Elves on Maurer's next turn.


Timo Schünemann 1 – 1 Lukas Maurer


### Game 3


For the deciding game, Schünemann once again kept his seven while Maurer mulliganed ... first to six cards without land, then to: [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest), [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote), [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) double Elvish Visionay, which he kept.



![](http://media.wizards.com/legacy/migration/GHENT_final_schunemann.jpg)

*Timo Schünemann* 
Schünemann started on [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), Maurer on [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote). On turn two, Schünemann had [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish) and picked [Pyroclasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyroclasm) from his sideboard. Maurer missed on land (or one-drop) and passed without play.


Schünemann's [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) let him see what was going on in Maurer's hand, which had grown by one unhelpful [Priest of Titania](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Priest+of+Titania) and one [Ezuri, Renegade Leader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ezuri%2C+Renegade+Leader) in the meantime. Next turn, [Dark Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Ritual) and [Cabal Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Ritual) provided the mana—and [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) provided the extra cards. The game ended in flurry of Rituals and mana artifacts with another [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish) getting [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony) for way more loss of life than Maurer could afford to lose.


Congratulations to Timo Schünemann, winner of Grand Prix Ghent 2012!



Final - Timo Schünemann vs. Lukas Maurer
----------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke* 
 


![Omniscience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Omniscience)


 

### 5. [Omniscience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Omniscience)


In the end the now infamous [Omniscience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Omniscience) deck came short a couple of wins, but it did put two of its three pilots into day two, and was one of the early big stories of the tournament. Dumping the ten-mana enchantment onto the battlefield as early as turn one with the help of [Ancient Tomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Tomb), [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal), and [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), former PT champ Simon Görtzen and former GP champ Florian Koch surprised quite a few of their opponents. And casting [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn) for free is obviously so much nicer than simply putting it on the table by other means.


  
  
  
  

 
 


![Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wasteland)


 

### 4. [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)


Hardly anyone ever talks about this card anymore, for pretty much the same reason you don't constantly talk about air or sunshine: people simply take those things for granted. But there may not be another card in the Legacy format whose influence is more pervasive. Whenever people construct a mana base or try to figure out how much mana they can expect to have on which turn of the game, [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) is always a factor that can only be ignored at one's own peril.


  
  
  
  

 
 


![Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Terminus)


 

### 3. [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus)


Bolstered by a strong match-up against the ever-popular Maverick and against the increasing numbers of tribal decks, UW Miracles proved to be a real player this weekend, maybe even a mover or shaker. [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus) certainly shakes things up and moves cards around. Thanks in large part to the one-mana [Wrath of God](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wrath+of+God), Legacy finally has a genuine control deck again. Players like Hall of Famer Raphaël Lévy, Max Sjöblom, and Andrea Milillo chose the deck, and the latter two both made it all the way to the Top 8 with it.


  
  
  
  

 
 


![Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wirewood+Symbiote)


 

### 2. [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote)


[Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote) may not be the most flashy card in the Elf deck, that title probably belongs to [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) or maybe [Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid). But [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote) does so many things, protecting its Elf friends from removal, untapping them, having them block opposing creatures with [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) all day, or simply returning [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) to one's hand for an additional card, because sometimes all it takes is one additional card. Throughout the weekend we've seen many Elf decks doing amazing things with [Wirewood Symbiote](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wirewood+Symbiote) all through to the final where.


  
  
  
  

 
 


![Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gitaxian+Probe)


 

### 1. [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe)


When looking at [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe), storm combo does not immediately come to mind, but that's where the card did its best work during this Grand Prix. In champion Timo Schünemann's [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) deck [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) provided an extra spell for storm, an extra card in the graveyard to achieve threshold for [Cabal Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Ritual), not to mention that he was able to look at his opponents' hands, allowing him to better time his many discard spells, to better aim his [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy), and to know when the way was clear for his combo kill. All at the top bargain price of no card investment and no mana investment at all. Deal!
